Two Hadiths Warning Against Hasty Takfir
Ibn Asakir narrates two hadiths warning against falsely accusing Muslims of kufr and shirk.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the severity of falsely accusing a Muslim of disbelief (takfir) as demonstrated in two prophetic hadiths.

Core Idea
Hasty takfir is a grave sin; the Prophet warned against it with strong words.

The danger of declaring a Muslim a disbeliever without clear proof is one of the most serious issues in Islamic theology. Imam Ibn Asakir, in his defense of orthodoxy, narrates two powerful hadiths that illustrate the Prophet's own warnings against this practice. These hadiths serve as a reminder that faith is not to be judged lightly, and that even a simple affirmation of Islamic statements can protect a person from the charge of kufr.

Guided Path
1
Read the two hadiths
Read the Arabic text of both hadiths and their literal translations. Notice the different scenarios: the first involves a Quran reciter who attacks a neighbor, the second involves a young man passing by.
Pay attention to the companions' reactions and the Prophet's responses.
2
Identify the key warnings
In the first hadith, the Prophet says the shooter (accuser) is more deserving of punishment. In the second, Abu Huraira emphasizes that testifying against a Muslim without qualification leads to the Fire.
These warnings underscore the gravity of false takfir.
3
Reflect on the Companions' caution
Note how Abu Huraira immediately confronted the accuser and personally verified the young man's faith by asking about prayer and statements of tawhid.
The young man's affirmation of 'Subhan Allah' and 'La ilaha illa Allah' was accepted as evidence of faith.
4
Apply the lesson
Consider how these hadiths guide us in our own judgments. We must never call a Muslim a kafir without overwhelming evidence, and even then, it is a serious matter best left to scholars.
The Prophet's warnings remind us that false testimony of disbelief is itself a sin that incurs Hellfire.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صلى الله عليه وسلم ( إن مما أخاف عليكم بعدى رجل قرأ كتاب الله عز وجل حتى إذا رؤيت عليه بهجته وكان ردءا للإسلام اغتره ذلك إلى ما شاء الله فانسلخ منه وخرج على جاره بالسيف وشهد عليه بالشرك قلنا يا رسول الله من أولى بها المرمى أو الرامي قال بل الرامي ) . وأخبرنا الشيخان أبو عبد الله محمد بن الفضل بن أحمد الفراوى وأبو المظفر عبد المنعم بن عبد الكريم بن هوازن النيسابوريان بها قالا أنا أبو سعيد محمد بن علی بن محمد الصوفى المعروف بالخشاب قال أنا أبو بكر محمد بن عبد الله بن محمد بن زكريا الجوزقي ، قال أنا أبو العباس محمد ابن عبد الرحمن ابن محمد الدغولى ، قال أنا أحمد بن إبراهيم بن حرب . النيسابوري قال ثنا يزيد ابن هارون قال ثنا جهير بن يزيد العبدى عن خداش بن عياش ، قال كنت فى حلقة بالكوفة إذا رجل يحدث قال كنا جلوسا مع أبي هريرة فمر فتى فقال رجل من الحلقة هذا كافر من أهل النار فقام أبو هريرة حتى أتى الفتى فقال من أنت قال أنا فلان بن فلان قال رحم الله أباك ، قال فجعل الفتى يلتفت فقال إلام تلتفت قال لم أصل قال وتصلى ، فقال سبحان الله فقال وتقول سبحان الله، قال لا إله إلا الله قال وتقول لا إله إلا الله ، فقال ما أريد أنى تركت الصلاة وإن لى ما على وجه الأرض قال رحمك الله رحمك الله رحمك الله ، ثم جاء حتى أخذ مجلسه فقال سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول : ( من شهد على مسلم بشهادة ليس لها بأهل فليتبوأ مقعده من النار )
May peace be upon him: 'Indeed, among the things I fear for you after me is a man who recites the Book of Allah, until when his beauty is seen upon him and he becomes a support for Islam, that deceives him to whatever Allah wills, then he sheds it and goes out against his neighbor with the sword and testifies against him with shirk.' We said: 'O Messenger of Allah, who is more deserving of it, the target or the shooter?' He said: 'Rather, the shooter.' And the two shaykhs reported to us ... (chain) ... said: I was in a gathering in Kufa when a man was narrating. He said: We were sitting with Abu Huraira when a young man passed by. A man from the gathering said: 'This one is a disbeliever, an inhabitant of the Fire.' So Abu Huraira stood until he reached the young man. He said: 'Who are you?' He said: 'So-and-so, son of so-and-so.' He said: 'May Allah have mercy on your father.' He said: Then the young man started looking around. He said: 'What are you looking at?' He said: 'I haven't prayed.' He said: 'Do you pray?' He said: 'Subhan Allah.' He said: 'And do you say Subhan Allah?' He said: 'La ilaha illa Allah.' He said: 'And do you say La ilaha illa Allah?' He said: 'I do not intend that I have left prayer, and I have whatever is on the face of the earth.' He said: 'May Allah have mercy on you, may Allah have mercy on you, may Allah have mercy on you.' Then he came until he took his seat and said: 'I heard the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, say: "Whoever testifies against a Muslim with a testimony he is not qualified for, let him take his seat in the Fire."'
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage presents two hadiths. The first hadith is narrated by the Prophet (peace be upon him) warning about a man who recites the Quran and appears to be a support for Islam, but then becomes deceived, sheds the Quran, attacks his Muslim neighbor with a sword, and testifies against him with shirk. The companions asked who is more deserving: the target (the one being attacked) or the shooter (the one doing the attack). The Prophet replied that the shooter is more deserving (meaning more sinful). This serves as a severe warning about the grave sin of apostasy and false accusation of shirk. The second hadith is narrated through a chain from Abu Huraira. In his presence, a young man passed by and someone in the gathering declared him to be a disbeliever, destined for hell. Abu Huraira immediately approached the young man and asked him about his identity, then inquired if he prayed. The young man responded by saying 'Subhan Allah' and 'La ilaha illa Allah', indicating his faith. Abu Huraira then prayed for him three times and returned to his seat, narrating the hadith: 'Whoever testifies against a Muslim with a testimony he is not qualified for, let him prepare his seat in the Fire.' This demonstrates the caution of the Companions against unjustified takfir, and that affirming the basic testimonies of faith is sufficient to ward off the charge of disbelief. Together, these two hadiths emphasize the gravity of declaring a Muslim a kafir without clear grounds.

Key Terms
تكفير
شهادة
شرك
رمي
شهد
مسلم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A single act of prayer or dhikr is insufficient to prove faith; one must demonstrate consistent practice.
Correction: The hadith shows Abu Huraira accepted the young man's statements of 'Subhan Allah' and 'La ilaha illa Allah' as proof of his faith, indicating that a person who affirms Islamic testimonies should not be declared a disbeliever.

Checkpoint
What did Abu Huraira do when someone in the gathering called a passing young man a kafir?
A) He ignored the comment
B) He interrogated the young man about his prayer and statements of faith
C) He agreed and added evidence
D) He left the gathering

Key Takeaway
False testimony of disbelief is a major sin that leads to the Fire; one must be extremely cautious in declaring a Muslim a kafir.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever, even in your heart, judged another Muslim as less of a believer because of a sin you observed? How does the Prophet's statement that 'the shooter is more deserving' confront that attitude? Will you actively replace that judgment with mercy and prayer for them starting today?
?
In the second hadith, Abu Huraira did not assume the worst but personally checked the young man's faith. Think of a person you have dismissed as religiously insincere. When will you go out of your way to ask them about their faith and affirm even the smallest sign of iman?
?
The young man said he has 'whatever is on the face of the earth'—meaning he valued nothing more than his faith. Is there anything in your life—wealth, status, relationships—that you would weigh against your Islam? What is needed today to give your iman that supreme value?

Companions on Refusing Takfir
Three narrations on refusing takfir from Ibn Umar and Jabir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Companions avoided declaring Muslims kafir, emphasizing the power of the shahada to refute false accusations of shirk and kufr.

Core Idea
The shahada protects a Muslim from accusations of kufr.

These three narrations from Ibn Umar and Jabir illustrate the Companions' extreme caution in declaring anyone a kafir. When someone complained about being called a mushrik, Ibn Umar's immediate response was to affirm the power of 'La ilaha illa Allah'. The passage shows that uttering the shahada is sufficient to refute false accusations of disbelief.

Guided Path
1
Read the three stories
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the chain of narrators but focus on the responses of Ibn Umar and Jabir.
The isnad is not essential for the lesson.
2
Identify the common response
In the first two stories, Ibn Umar tells the complainants to say 'La ilaha illa Allah'. Notice how this simple utterance disproves the accusation.
3
Analyze Jabir's reaction
Jabir is asked if the Companions ever called anyone from the people of the qibla a mushrik or kafir. Observe his strong denial and alarm.
His reaction shows how serious takfir was considered.
4
Reflect on the lesson
Consider the principle that as long as a person affirms tawheed, they are not to be declared kafir by others, regardless of accusations.
This guards against extremism in takfir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأخبرنا الشيخ أبو القسم إسماعيل بن أحمد بن السمرقندي قال أنا أبو الحسين أحمد بن محمد بن أحمد بن النقور قال ثنا أبو القسم عيسى ابن علی بن عيسى الوزير أملاء قال ثنا أبو القسم عبد الله بن محمد بن عبد العزيز قال حدثنا زيد بن آخزم قال ثنا أبو قتيبة قال ثنا منصور بن دينار عن عبيد الله بن عمر عن نافع ، أن رجلاً قال لابن عمر أن لي جاراً يشهد على بالشرك فقال قل لا إله إلا الله تكذبه . وأخبرنا الشيخ أبو الفرج سعيد بن أبى الرجاء بن أبي منصور الصيرفي بأصبهان قال أنا أبو الفتح منصور بن الحسين بن على بن القسم بن الرواد الكاتب ، وأبو طاهر أحمد بن محمود بن أحمد الثقفي الأديب قالا أنا أبو بكر محمد بن إبراهيم بن على بن عاصم بن المقرى ، قال ثنا أبو محمد جعفر بن أحمد الربعي ، قال ثنا أحمد بن جعفر المعقرى ، قال ثنا النضر بن محمد قال ثنا عكرمة ، يعنى ابن عمار قال ثنا سوار بن شبيب الأعرجي قال كنت قاعداً عند ابن عمر فجاء رجل فقال يابن عمر أن أقواماً يشهدون علينا بالكفر والشرك فقال ويلك أفلا قلت لا إله إلا الله قال فقال أهل البيت لا إله إلا الله حتى ارتج البيت . أخبرنا أبو الفضل محمد بن إسماعيل بن الفضل الفضيلي قال أنا أبو القسم أحمد بن محمد بن محمد الخليلي ببلخ قال أنا أبو القسم على ابن أحمد بن محمد بن الحسن الخزاعى قال أنا أبو سعيد الهيثم بن كليب الشاشي قال ثنا ابن عفان العامري قال ثنا ابن نمير قال ثنا الأعمش عن أبي سفيان قال أتينا جابر بن عبد الله وكان مجاوراً بمكة وكان نازلاً في بنى فهر فسأله رجل فقال هل كنتم تدعون أحداً من أهل القبلة مشركاً ، قال معاذ الله وفزع لذلك ، قال هل كنتم أظنه تدعونه كافرا قال لا
And the shaykh Abu al-Qasim Isma'il ibn Ahmad al-Samarqandi informed us ... from Nafi' that a man said to Ibn Umar: 'I have a neighbor who testifies against me with shirk.' He said: 'Say: La ilaha illa Allah, and he will lie.' And the shaykh Abu al-Faraj Sa'id ibn Abi al-Raja' al-Sayrafi in Isfahan informed us ... that Suwar ibn Shabib al-A'araji said: I was sitting with Ibn Umar when a man came and said: 'O Ibn Umar, some people testify against us with kufr and shirk.' He said: 'Woe to you! Why don't you say La ilaha illa Allah?' He said: Then the people of the house said La ilaha illa Allah until the house shook. And Abu al-Fadl Muhammad ibn Isma'il informed us ... from Abu Sufyan: We came to Jabir ibn Abdullah and he was residing in Mecca and staying in the tribe of Fihr. A man asked him: 'Did you used to call anyone from the people of the qibla a mushrik?' He said: 'I seek refuge with Allah!' and was alarmed by that. He said: 'Did you used to call him a kafir?' He said: 'No.'
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage contains three narrations that illustrate the Companions' extreme caution regarding takfir. The first narration: A man complains to Ibn Umar that his neighbor testifies that he (the man) is a mushrik. Ibn Umar's response is simple: 'Say La ilaha illa Allah, and he will lie.' This implies that the testimony is false because the man's utterance of the shahada proves his faith. The second narration: Another man comes to Ibn Umar complaining that people testify against them with kufr and shirk. Ibn Umar questions him: 'Woe to you! Why don't you say La ilaha illa Allah?' When the man says it, the entire household echoes it until the house shakes, emphasizing the power of this declaration. The third narration: Jabir ibn Abdullah is asked whether the Companions ever called anyone from the people of the qibla (i.e., Muslims) a mushrik or a kafir. He reacts with strong denial and alarm, saying 'I seek refuge with Allah!' and firmly says 'No.' These stories demonstrate that the Companions considered the mere profession of tawheed as sufficient evidence of faith and would not accuse a Muslim of kufr or shirk lightly.

Key Terms
لا إله إلا الله
تكفير
أهل القبلة
شرك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A person can be declared kafir based on sinful behavior or accusations from others, even if they affirm tawheed.
Correction: The Companions taught that as long as a person says 'La ilaha illa Allah', they are not to be called kafir, because the shahada is the proof of faith.

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Umar, what should a person do if someone falsely testifies against him with shirk?
A) Fight the accuser
B) Say 'La ilaha illa Allah' to disprove the testimony
C) Seek revenge
D) Leave the area

Key Takeaway
The Companions refused to declare anyone who says La ilaha illa Allah a kafir, regardless of accusations.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you quick to label someone as a disbeliever because of a sin or a difference of opinion? How would the Companions' response in these narrations change your attitude toward fellow Muslims you disagree with? What will you do the next time you feel the urge to accuse someone of kufr?
?
The second narration shows the man's household echoing 'La ilaha illa Allah' until the house shakes. When was the last time you felt that deep, shaking conviction in your own declaration of faith? What does this story reveal about the power of that simple phrase, and how can you revive that power in your daily life?
?
Jabir was alarmed by the mere suggestion that the Companions called anyone a mushrik. If someone were to ask you about a Muslim you know who commits a grave sin, would you be equally alarmed at the thought of calling them a kafir? What is holding you back from having that same caution?

Forbidding Takfir and Defending Ibn Kullab on Divine Speech
Ibn Asakir concludes that takfir is forbidden and defends Ibn Kullab's position on divine speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ibn Asakir forbids declaring Muslims disbelievers and how he defends Ibn Kullab’s position on the nature of divine speech.

Core Idea
Takfir is a grave sin; misunderstanding divine speech led to unfair accusations.

Ibn Asakir concludes his work with a firm principle: the hadith forbid declaring Muslims disbelievers. He then applies this principle by defending Ibn Kullab, a Sunni theologian wrongly accused of innovation. The defense includes a crucial clarification about Allah's speech—it is eternal and not restricted to temporal descriptions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the two main points
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice that it first states a prohibition of takfir and then defends Ibn Kullab's theological view.
The passage is a single continuous argument.
2
Understand the prohibition of takfir
Ibn Asakir declares that the preceding reports forbid declaring Muslims disbelievers. Whoever does so disobeys the Prophet (peace be upon him).
This is a strong warning against hasty takfir.
3
Examine the historical case of al-Ahwazi
Ibn Asakir notes that al-Ahwazi's takfir of Ibn Kullab was influenced by Mu'tazili ideas, showing the danger of following deviant trends.
Al-Ahwazi is not further identified here.
4
Learn the defense of Ibn Kullab
Through Ibn Abi Zaid's letter, it is shown that the accusation of innovation against Ibn Kullab lacks evidence. Ibn Kullab's view on divine speech is clarified: command, prohibition, and news are temporal descriptions, not eternal attributes.
Ibn Kullab is identified as an imam of Sunni theology.
5
Appreciate the theological nuance
The clarification aligns with reason and revelation: Allah's speech in eternity is one perfect attribute, while its commanded/prohibited/informing aspects appear when revealed to creatures.
This resolves an apparent tension in divine attribute understanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فهذه الأخبار تمنع من تكفير المسلمين فمن أقدم على التكفير فقد عصى سيد المرسلين ، وإنما اقتدى الأهوازي في تكفيره إياه وتهمته بالضلال بقول من كثره من القائلين بمذاهب أهل الاعتزال، وقد قرأت بخط على ابن بقاء الوراق المحدث المصرى رسالة كتب بها أبو محمد عبد الله بن أبي زيد القيرواني الفقيه المالكي وكان مقدم أصحاب مالك رحمه الله بالمغرب في زمانه إلى على بن أحمد بن إسماعيل البغدادي المعتزلى جواباً عن رسالة كتب بها إلى المالكيين من أهل القيروان يظهر نصيحتهم بما يدخلهم به فى أقاويل أهل الاعتزال فذكر الرسالة بطولها في جزء وهى معروفة فمن جملة جواب ابن أبي زيد له أن قال : ونسبت ابن كلاب (1) إلى البدعة ثم لم تحك عنه قولا يعرف أنه بدعة (1) بضم الكاف وتشديد اللام وهو الإمام أبو محمد عبد الله بن سعيد القطان المتوفى بعد سنة أربعين ومأتين ويقال أنه أخو يحيى بن القطان إمام الجرح والتعديل كان إمام متكلمة السنة في عهد أحمد وممن يرافق الحارث بن أسد ، ويشنع عليه بعض الضعفاء في أصول الدين ما ينسب إليه من أن كلام الله لا يوصف بكونه أمراً ونبياً أو خبراً مع أنه يعنى بذلك أن وصف الكلام بأحدها إنما هو بعد الوحى والتنزيل حيث يبلغ المأمور والمنهى والخبر لا أنها أوصاف إضافية للكلام يوصف بها عند التبليغ وأما باعتبار وجوده العلمي في ذات الله تعالى فالواحد الأحد ليس علمه بطريق الارتسام والحصول ، بل علمه حضوری وحدانى وهكذا باقي صفاته جل جلاله ، وهذا كلام ليس ببعيد عن الشرع والعقل
So these reports prevent declaring Muslims disbelievers. So whoever takes the step of declaring takfir has disobeyed the Master of the Messengers. And al-Ahwazi only followed in his takfir of him and his accusation of misguidance the saying of many who advocate the doctrines of the Mu'tazila. And I have read in the handwriting of Ali ibn Baqa' al-Warraq, the Egyptian hadith scholar, a letter sent by Abu Muhammad Abdullah ibn Abi Zaid al-Qayrawani, the Maliki jurist, who was the foremost of the Malikis in the Maghrib in his time, to Ali ibn Ahmad ibn Ismail al-Baghdadi al-Mu'tazili, as a response to a letter he had sent to the Malikis of Qayrawan, pretending to give them advice by introducing them to the sayings of the Mu'tazila. So he mentioned the letter in full in a volume, and it is well known. Among the points of Ibn Abi Zaid's response, he said: 'You attributed Ibn Kullab to innovation, but then you did not report a statement from him that is known to be an innovation. (1) (Ibn Kullab) with dammah on the kaf and tashdid on the lam: he is the Imam Abu Muhammad Abdullah ibn Sa'id al-Qattan, who died after the year 240 AH. It is said he was the brother of Yahya ibn Sa'id al-Qattan, the Imam of jarh and ta'dil. He was the imam of the theologians of the Sunnah in the time of Ahmad, and among those who accompanied al-Harith ibn Asad. Some weak people attack him in the principles of religion for what is attributed to him that the speech of Allah is not described as command, prohibition, or news, meaning that the description of speech with any of these is only after revelation and sending down, when the commanded, forbidden, and informed reach. But in terms of its eternal existence in the Essence of Allah, the One, the Unique, His knowledge is not by way of impression and acquisition, but His knowledge is presential and unitary, and similarly the rest of His attributes, exalted be His Majesty. And this statement is not far from the Shari'ah and reason.'
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage is the author's concluding analysis. He first states unequivocally that the preceding hadith and athar forbid declaring Muslims kafir, and that anyone who does so has disobeyed the Prophet. He then connects this to a historical case: al-Ahwazi, who engaged in takfir, was influenced by the Mu'tazila. To further argue against hasty takfir and to defend a prominent Sunni theologian, Ibn Asakir cites a letter from Ibn Abi Zaid al-Qayrawani, a respected Maliki scholar, responding to a Mu'tazili. In that response, Ibn Abi Zaid defends Ibn Kullab, who was accused of innovation. He notes that the accuser could not cite any known statement from Ibn Kullab that is actually an innovation. He then provides a biographical note on Ibn Kullab, identifying him as a great imam of theology in the time of Ahmad ibn Hanbal, and clarifies the accusation: Ibn Kullab is said to hold that Allah's speech is not described as command, prohibition, or news. Ibn Abi Zaid explains that this is a misunderstanding; Ibn Kullab meant that these descriptions apply only after revelation (when the commanded and prohibited are addressed to people). In the eternal divine essence, the attribute of speech is unitary and not divisible into such categories, just as Allah's knowledge is presential and not acquired. The author endorses this as being in harmony with both revelation and reason.

Key Terms
تكفير
أهل الاعتزال
ابن كلاب
كلام الله
صفات الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people thought Ibn Kullab denied that Allah's speech includes command, prohibition, or news entirely.
Correction: Ibn Kullab affirmed these descriptions apply to revelation (after the event), not to the eternal attribute of speech in Allah's essence.

Checkpoint
What did Ibn Abi Zaid say about the accusation that Ibn Kullab was an innovator?
A) He was indeed an innovator
B) His opinion was not known to be an innovation
C) He followed the Mu'tazila
D) He rejected the Quran

Key Takeaway
Declaring Muslims disbelievers is forbidden, and Ibn Kullab’s view on divine speech (as eternal, with temporal descriptions) is in harmony with Shari'ah and reason.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever mentally declared someone a 'deviant' or 'misguided' without deeply understanding their position, as al-Ahwazi did to Ibn Kullab? What would it cost you to seek clarification instead?
?
Ibn Abi Zaid defended Ibn Kullab despite the accusation being widespread. Is there a person or group you avoid defending because it is unpopular? Will you ask Allah for courage to stand for truth even when it is uncomfortable?
?
This lesson teaches that takfir is disobedience to the Prophet. Search your heart: have you ever considered someone outside the fold of Islam based on a misunderstanding? What concrete step will you take today to repent from that and learn proper boundaries of faith?

Defense of Ibn Kullab: His Orthodox Stance on Divine Speech
Ibn Abi Zayd defends Ibn Kullab from accusations of innovation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ibn Abi Zayd defends Ibn Kullab from accusations of innovation by explaining his view on divine speech and affirming his adherence to the Sunna.

Core Idea
Ibn Kullab's view on God's speech is orthodox, not heretical.

Ibn Abi Zayd al-Qayrawani refutes a Mu'tazili who accused Ibn Kullab of innovation. He first clarifies Ibn Kullab's nuanced position on divine speech, showing it aligns with reason and revelation. Then he asserts that Ibn Kullab was a defender of the Sunna who refuted the Jahmiyya.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the accusations
Read the Arabic passage once. Notice that Ibn Abi Zayd addresses two accusations: that Ibn Kullab holds a problematic view on divine speech and that he is an innovator.
The passage begins with 'You attributed to Ibn Kullab innovation...'
2
Understand Ibn Kullab's position on divine speech
Ibn Abi Zayd explains that Ibn Kullab's statement that God's speech is not command, prohibition, or report until revelation means these descriptions apply only after revelation, not to the eternal attribute.
The key is that Ibn Kullab distinguishes between the eternal attribute and its temporal manifestations.
3
Note the defense of orthodoxy
Ibn Abi Zayd concludes that this view is not far from law and reason, and then denies the innovation charge by highlighting Ibn Kullab's role as a refuter of heretics.
This shows that Ibn Kullab was a mainstream Sunni figure, not a deviant.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإنما اقندى الأهوازي في تكفيره إياه وتهمته بالضلال بقول من كثره من القائلين بماذاهب أهل الاعتزال، وقد قرأت بخط على ابن بقاء الوراق المحدث المصرى رسالة كتب بها أبو محمد عبد الله بن أبي زيد القيرواني الفقيه المالكي وكان مقدم أصحاب مالك رحمه الله بالمغرب في زمانه إلى على بن أحمد بن إسماعيل البغدادي المعتزلى جواباً عن رسالة كتب بها إلى المالكيين من أهل القيروان يظهر نصيحتهم بما يدخلهم به فى أقاويل أهل الاعتزال فذكر الرسالة بطولها في جزء وهى معروفة فمن جملة جواب ابن أبي زيد له أن قال : ونسبت ابن كلاب إلى البدعة ثم لم تحك عنه قولا يعرف أنه بدعة وهو الإمام أبو محمد عبد الله بن سعيد القطان المتوفى بعد سنة أربعين ومأتين ويقال أنه أخو يحيى بن القطان إمام الجرح والتعديل كان إمام متكلمة السنة في عهد أحمد وممن يرافق الحارث بن أسد ، ويشنع عليه بعض الضعفاء في أصول الدين ما ينسب إليه من أن كلام الله لا يوصف بكونه أمراً ونبياً أو خبراً مع أنه يعنى بذلك أن وصف الكلام بأحدها إنما هو بعد الوحى والتنزيل حيث يبلغ المأمور والمنهى والخبر لا أنها أوصاف إضافية للكلام يوصف بها عند التبليغ وأما باعتبار وجوده العلمي في ذات الله تعالى فالواحد الأحد ليس علمه بطريق الارتسام والحصول ، بل علمه حضوری وحدانى وهكذا باقي صفاته جل جلاله ، وهذا كلام ليس ببعيد عن الشرع والعقل فيوسم بهذا الاسم ، وما علمنا من نسب إلى ابن كلاب البدعة والذى بلغنا أنه يتقلد السنة ويتولى الرد على الجهمية وغيرهم من أهل البدع ، یعنی عبد الله بن سعيد بن كلاب وذكرت الاشعرى فنسبته إلى الكفر وقلت أنه كان مشهوراً بالكفر وهذا ما علمنا أن أحداً رماه بالكفر غيرك هذا ولم تذكر الذي كفر به وكيف يكون مشهوراً بالكفر من لم ينسب إليه أحد علمناه في عصره ، ولا بعد عصره ، وقلت أنه قدم بغداد ولم يقرب أحداً من المالكين ولا من آل حماد بن زيد لعلمه أنهم يعتقدون أنه کافر ، ولم تذكر ما الذى كفروه به
And the Ahwazi only followed in declaring him a disbeliever and accusing him of misguidance the statement of many of those who follow the doctrines of the Mu'tazila. I have read in the handwriting of 'Ali ibn Baqa' al-Warraq, the Egyptian hadith specialist, a letter written by Abu Muhammad 'Abdullah ibn Abi Zayd al-Qayrawani, the Maliki jurist—who was the foremost of the companions of Malik, may Allah have mercy on him, in the Maghrib in his time—to 'Ali ibn Ahmad ibn Isma'il al-Baghdadi al-Mu'tazili, in response to a letter he had written to the Malikis of Qayrawan in which he pretended to advise them by causing them to enter into the doctrines of the Mu'tazila. He mentioned the letter in its entirety in a volume, and it is well known. Among the response of Ibn Abi Zayd to him, he said: 'You attributed to Ibn Kullab innovation, then you did not report from him a statement known to be innovation. He is the Imam Abu Muhammad 'Abdullah ibn Sa'id al-Qattan, who died after the year two hundred and forty, and it is said that he was the brother of Yahya ibn Sa'id al-Qattan, the imam of jarh and ta'dil. He was the imam of the speaking scholars of the Sunna in the era of Ahmad, and among those who associated with al-Harith ibn Asad. Some weak people criticize him in matters of the principles of religion for what is attributed to him: that the speech of Allah is not described as being a command, a prohibition, or a report—even though he meant by that that describing speech as one of these is only after revelation and sending down, when the commanded, the forbidden, and the reported are conveyed; not that these are additional attributes of speech by which it is described at the time of conveying. But with regard to its existence as knowledge in the essence of Allah the Exalted, the One, the Unique, His knowledge is not by way of mental impression and acquisition, but rather His knowledge is present and unitary, and likewise the rest of His attributes, glorified is His Majesty. This is speech not far from the Law and reason, so he is marked with this name. We do not know who attributed innovation to Ibn Kullab, and what has reached us is that he adhered to the Sunna and undertook refutation of the Jahmiyya and other people of innovation—meaning 'Abdullah ibn Sa'id ibn Kullab. And you mentioned al-Ash'ari and attributed him to disbelief and claimed that he was notorious for disbelief, but we do not know that anyone accused him of disbelief besides you. And you did not mention what he did to be considered a disbeliever. How can one be notorious for disbelief when no one we know in his time or after his time attributed it to him? And you claimed that he came to Baghdad and did not approach any of the Malikis or the family of Hammad ibn Zaid because he knew that they considered him a disbeliever—but you did not mention what they considered him a disbeliever for.'
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazili 'Ali ibn Ahmad al-Baghdadi's accusations against Ibn Kullab and al-Ash'ari. The author first explains that the Ahwazi's takfir is based on following the Mu'tazila. Then he cites from a letter by the Maliki scholar Ibn Abi Zayd al-Qayrawani, who defends Ibn Kullab as an Imam of the Sunna. Ibn Abi Zayd explains that Ibn Kullab's statement about God's speech not being described as command, prohibition, etc. until revelation is metaphorical, referring to the attributes of speech in relation to conveying commands, not to the eternal attribute of speech in God's essence. He argues that this view is not far from the Law and reason. He then denies that Ibn Kullab is an innovator, stating that he was a defender of the Sunna and a refuter of the Jahmiyya. Regarding al-Ash'ari, Ibn Abi Zayd questions the claim that he was notorious for disbelief, noting that no one except the Mu'tazili made such an accusation. He further argues that al-Ash'ari's not approaching the Malikis does not prove disbelief, and that the Mu'tazili did not specify what specific belief rendered him a disbeliever. The lesson thus defends both scholars from unfounded accusations.

Key Terms
ابن كلاب
بدعة
كلام الله
جهمية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ibn Kullab denied that God's speech is eternal by saying it is not command, prohibition, or report.
Correction: Ibn Abi Zayd explains that Ibn Kullab meant these descriptions apply only after revelation, not that the eternal attribute itself is such.

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Abi Zayd, what did Ibn Kullab mean by saying God's speech is not command, prohibition, or report?
A) Speech is created
B) These descriptions only apply after revelation
C) God does not speak
D) Speech is an accident

Key Takeaway
Ibn Kullab's position on divine speech is orthodox and his refutation of the Jahmiyya shows his commitment to the Sunna.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever judged a scholar's position based on a secondhand report without verifying it directly from their own words? What step will you take this week to seek out and understand a perspective you have been quick to dismiss?
?

When you encounter someone whose theological stance seems questionable, do you first assume ignorance or innovation, or do you try to understand their reasoning? How can you cultivate a more balanced approach like Ibn Abi Zayd?
?
The passage highlights the danger of mislabeling a believer as an innovator. Is there anyone in your life—a scholar, teacher, or fellow Muslim—whom you have labeled unfairly based on incomplete knowledge? How can you rectify that today?

Defense of al-Ash'ari: Rebutting Accusations of Disbelief
Ibn Abi Zayd refutes the Mu'tazili's accusation of disbelief against al-Ash'ari.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ibn Abi Zayd refutes the claim that al-Ash'ari was a disbeliever and challenges the Mu'tazili's evidence.

Core Idea
The accusation of disbelief against al-Ash'ari has no basis and is unique to his Mu'tazili opponent.

Ibn Abi Zayd directly addresses the Mu'tazili's claim that al-Ash'ari was notorious for disbelief. He points out the lack of evidence and the absence of any such accusation from other scholars of the time, thus defending al-Ash'ari's orthodoxy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the accusation
Read the Arabic passage. Notice that the Mu'tazili claims al-Ash'ari was notorious for disbelief and avoided the Malikis.
The passage begins with 'And you mentioned al-Ash'ari...'
2
Analyze Ibn Abi Zayd's rebuttal
He questions why no one else accused al-Ash'ari and why the Mu'tazili did not specify the cause of disbelief. He dismisses the claim about avoiding Malikis as unsubstantiated.
The rebuttal relies on the lack of corroboration and evidence.
3
Understand the logical argument
The accusation is invalid because it is unsupported and the accuser fails to provide proof. Ibn Abi Zayd's method is to demand clarity and evidence.
This is a common pattern in polemical refutations.

Defending Ibn Kullab and al-Ash'ari from Baseless Accusations
Ibn Abi Zayd refutes claims that Ibn Kullab was a bid'ati and Ash'ari a kafir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ibn Abi Zayd refutes accusations of bid'a and kufr against early theologians by demanding specific evidence and noting the absence of widespread condemnation.

Core Idea
Baseless takfir is refuted by demanding evidence and noting the silence of the scholarly community.

Ibn Abi Zayd al-Qayrawani, a Maliki scholar, responds to an anonymous critic who accused Ibn Kullab of innovation and al-Ash'ari of unbelief. In this passage, he dismantles these allegations by pointing out the lack of evidence and the fact that no other scholars made such claims. This lesson examines his method of defense, which hinges on two key principles: the necessity of specifying the act that constitutes bid'a or kufr, and the historical absence of such accusations from the broader scholarly tradition.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the structure: Ibn Abi Zayd first addresses the accusation against Ibn Kullab, then turns to al-Ash'ari. Pay attention to the rhetorical questions he uses.
The passage is a refutation, not a neutral description.
2
Identify the two accusations
Find where the critic's claims are stated: that Ibn Kullab was a bid'ati and that al-Ash'ari was a kafir. Then see how Ibn Abi Zayd responds to each.
Ibn Abi Zayd does not repeat the accusations verbatim; he paraphrases them.
3
Analyze the refutation strategies
For Ibn Kullab: he counters by stating his reputation as a defender of the Sunna. For al-Ash'ari: he points out the lack of evidence, the uniqueness of the accusation, and the critic's failure to specify the cause of kufr.
Notice the pattern: refutation by counter-evidence and by questioning the accuser's evidence.
4
Reflect on the broader lesson
Consider why this method is important in Islamic theology: it prevents reckless takfir and protects the integrity of scholarly discourse.
This connects to the principle that accusations must be substantiated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فیوسم بهذا الاسم ، وما علمنا من نسب إلى ابن كلاب البدعة (۱) والذى بلغنا أنه يتقلد السنة ويتولى الرد على الجهمية وغيرهم من أهل البدع ، یعنی عبد الله بن سعيد بن كلاب وذكرت الاشعرى فنسبته إلى الكفر وقلت أنه كان مشهوراً بالكفر وهذا ما علمنا أن أحداً رماه بالكفر غيرك هذا ولم تذكر الذي كفر به وكيف يكون مشهوراً بالكفر من لم ينسب إليه أحد علمناه في عصره ، ولا بعد عصره ، وقلت أنه قدم بغداد ولم يقرب أحداً من المالكين ولا من آل حماد بن زيد لعلمه أنهم يعتقدون أنه کافر ، ولم تذكر ما الذى كفروه به
He is labeled with this name, and we do not know of anyone who attributed innovation (bid'a) to Ibn Kullab. What has reached us is that he adhered to the Sunna and undertook refutations of the Jahmiyya and other people of innovation, meaning Abdullah ibn Sa'id ibn Kullab. And you mentioned al-Ash'ari, attributing him to unbelief (kufr) and said that he was notorious for unbelief. This we do not know: that anyone accused him of unbelief besides you. And you did not mention that which he was accused of unbelief for. How can one be notorious for unbelief when no one known to us in his era or after his era attributed that to him? And you said that he came to Baghdad and did not approach any of the Malikis nor the family of Hammad ibn Zayd, because he knew that they considered him an unbeliever. And you did not mention what they accused him of unbelief for.
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage is a refutation argument. Ibn Abi Zayd is responding to an unnamed critic who accused Ibn Kullab of innovation (bid'a) and al-Ash'ari of unbelief (kufr). He begins by stating that Ibn Kullab is not known for bid'a; rather, he was a defender of the Sunna who refuted the Jahmiyya. Then he addresses the accusation against Ash'ari, emphasizing that no one in his time or after is known to have called him a kafir except this critic. He questions the basis of the accusation: the critic did not specify what act or belief constituted kufr, nor did he provide any evidence. The mention of Ash'ari not approaching the Malikis or the family of Hammad ibn Zayd is presented as the critic's own claim, but Ibn Abi Zayd notes that even that claim lacks specification of the actual cause of takfir. The overall argument is that takfir cannot be based on vague allegations.

Key Terms
ابن كلاب
البدعة
الكفر
الجهمية
أهل البدع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Ash'ari was widely considered a kafir by his contemporaries.
Correction: Ibn Abi Zayd argues that no known scholar in or after his time accused him of kufr except the critic, and the critic provided no specific evidence.

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Abi Zayd, what is the problem with the critic's accusation that Ash'ari was a kafir?
A) The critic did not provide evidence from the Quran
B) The critic did not specify what act or belief made him a kafir, and no one else made such an accusation
C) The critic was a known liar
D) Ash'ari repented before death

Key Takeaway
Accusations of bid'a and kufr must be supported by specific evidence and cannot be based on vague claims, especially when the accused is defended by credible scholars.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The critic accused al-Ash'ari without specifying the act of kufr. In your own life, when you hear someone accuse another of innovation or disbelief, do you immediately accept it or do you demand evidence? What will you do differently after learning from this passage?
?
This passage shows that baseless takfir is rejected by scholars. Will you commit to never uttering takfir of any Muslim unless you have clear proof as required by the scholars? What is one step you can take this week to ensure you speak justly about others' faith?

The Mu'tazili Inconsistency and Ash'ari's Stance on Takfir
Ibn Asakir defends Ash'ari by comparing the Mu'tazili's attack to a Rafidi's, stating Ash'ari's final stance on takfir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ibn Asakir defends al-Ash'ari against the Mu'tazili attack by highlighting inconsistency in the Mu'tazili position, and be able to state al-Ash'ari's final position on takfir regarding the lafz issue.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazili who creates the Qur'an has no standing to attack Ash'ari's view on created utterances.

Ibn Asakir presents a powerful analogy to expose the hypocrisy of the Mu'tazili critic. He then clarifies that al-Ash'ari's mature position was never to declare takfir on any Muslim over this issue. This passage is important for understanding the boundaries of takfir in Ash'ari theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal English translation. Let the author's argument come through.
The passage uses a strong analogy, so note the comparison.
2
Understand the analogy
Identify the analogy: the Mu'tazili criticizes al-Ash'ari for the lafz issue, yet himself holds a more extreme view (createdness of the Qur'an). This is like a Rafidi who curses the first three caliphs while criticizing another for speaking ill of Marwan.
The point is inconsistency and hypocrisy.
3
Identify al-Ash'ari's final stance
Find where Ibn Asakir states that al-Ash'ari did not declare takfir on anyone of the qibla, and that this was his final statement before death.
This is the key takeaway regarding takfir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما مثال تشنيع هذا المعتزلي الغليظ الفظ على أبي الحسن رحمه الله فى مسئلة اللفظ إلا كتشنيع رافضي على رجل من أهل السنة بتنقصه لمروان وهو يستجيز لنفسه لعن أبي بكر وعمر وعثمان الله عنهم ، لأن هذا المعتزلى وأهل مذهبه يدينون بخلق القرآن ، فكيف يشنع على من يرى خلق الألفاظ به والألحان ، ولكنه لما لم يتجاسر على إظهار ما كان يضمره ويدعو إليه منه موه على أهل المغرب بما ظنه يكون سبباً لنفورهم عنه ، فلم يلتفتوا لاستضلاعهم بالعلم إلى تمويهه ، ووجهوا قول الأشعرى فى اللفظ على أحسن وجوهه ، فإن قلد الأهوازي المعتزلة وأطلق القول بتكفيره لشدة جهله فإن الأشعري كان لا يرى تكفيره ولا تكفير أحد من أهل القبلة لسعة فضله ، وقد تقدمت عنه في ذلك حكاية زاهر بن أحمد وهى الحكاية التي ينبغي أن يصار إليها في التكفير ويعمد ، لأنه القول الأخير الذي مات عليه ، وأكثر المحققين من أصحابه رضي الله عنهم ذهب إليه
What is the example of this coarse, rude Mu'tazili's denunciation of Abu al-Hasan (may Allah have mercy on him) regarding the issue of utterance (lafz) except like the denunciation of a Rafidi against a man of Ahl al-Sunnah for his disparagement of Marwan, while he himself permits cursing Abu Bakr, 'Umar, and 'Uthman (may Allah be pleased with them)? Because this Mu'tazili and the people of his school profess the createdness of the Qur'an, so how can he denounce one who holds the createdness of utterances and sounds? But when he did not dare to reveal what he was concealing and calling to, he deceived the people of the Maghrib by what he thought would cause them to turn away from him. But they, due to their vast knowledge, did not pay attention to his deception, and they interpreted al-Ash'ari's statement about utterance (lafz) in the best possible ways. So if al-Ahwazi, following the Mu'tazila, went so far as to declare him a disbeliever due to his extreme ignorance, then al-Ash'ari did not hold him a disbeliever, nor anyone of the people of the qibla, due to his abundant merit. And the report from him on this matter has already preceded from Zahir ibn Ahmad, and it is the report that should be relied upon in (matters of) takfir and acted upon, because it is the final statement on which he died, and most of the verifiers among his companions (may Allah be pleased with them) adopted it.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage is an analogy and a defense. Ibn Asakir compares the Mu'tazili's attack on al-Ash'ari regarding the lafz issue to a Rafidi's attack on a Sunni for speaking ill of Marwan, while the Rafidi himself allows cursing the first three Caliphs. The point is that the Mu'tazili is inconsistent: he holds the Qur'an to be created, yet attacks Ash'ari who only holds utterances and sounds to be created. Ibn Asakir then explains that the Mu'tazili (al-Ahwazi) deceived the people of the Maghrib, but the scholars there saw through it and gave Ash'ari's words the best interpretation. Finally, he stresses that Ash'ari did not declare takfir on this matter or on anyone of the qibla, and his final position is the one transmitted by Zahir ibn Ahmad.

Key Terms
مسئلة اللفظ
خلق القرآن
خلق الألفاظ
التكفير
أهل القبلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Ash'ari declared takfir on those who held created utterances.
Correction: The passage states that al-Ash'ari did not declare takfir on anyone of the qibla, and his final statement was not to do so.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what was al-Ash'ari's position on declaring a person a disbeliever due to the lafz issue?
A) He declared them disbelievers
B) He did not declare them disbelievers
C) He was silent
D) He left it to the scholars

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari's final position was to not declare takfir on any Muslim over the issue of utterance (lafz).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Am I ever quick to judge another Muslim's belief while overlooking my own inconsistencies? This lesson shows the danger of hypocrisy—where do I see traces of that in my own heart? Today, I will commit to examining my own faults before criticizing others.
?
When I hear a difference of opinion among scholars, do I immediately assume the worst of one side? The scholars of the Maghrib took the best interpretation of al-Ash'ari's words. Are there people in my life whose views I have not given the benefit of the doubt? I will identify one person and actively seek the best understanding of their stance.
?
Al-Ash'ari's final position was to not declare takfir on anyone. Do I hold any ill feelings or judgments that effectively cut others off from the community of faith? How can I emulate his mercy and refrain from excommunication in matters where scholars disagreed? I will commit today to avoid labeling anyone as outside the fold of Islam over differences in non-essential matters.

Ash'ari Companions Refrain from Mutual Takfir
Ibn Asakir contrasts Ash'ari unity with sectarian disunity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ash'ari scholars, despite disagreeing on some issues, unanimously refrain from declaring each other disbelievers, contrasting with other sects.

Core Idea
Ash'aris differ but do not takfir; other sects takfir upon disagreement.

This passage from Ibn Asakir highlights a distinctive characteristic of the Ash'ari school: internal disagreements on subsidiary matters do not lead to mutual excommunication. Unlike other sects that readily declare each other disbelievers over differences, the Ash'ari companions remain united. Let's explore this contrast and its significance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the key terms: الأصحاب (companions), التكفير (declaring disbelief), and the names of other sects.
2
Identify the contrast
The passage explicitly contrasts the Ash'ari companions with other sects. List the differences: unity vs. mutual takfir, refraining vs. obligating disassociation.
3
Reflect on the cause
Ibn Asakir attributes this unity to a divine favor. Consider why internal disagreement does not lead to takfir among Ash'aris, unlike others.
This highlights the Ash'ari emphasis on core principles over subsidiary differences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما الأصحاب فإنهم مع اختلافهم فى بعض المسائل مجمعون على ترك تكفير بعضهم بعضا بخلاف من عداهم من سائر الطوائف ، وجميع الفرق فإنهم حين اختلفت بهم مستشنعات الأهواء والطرق كفر بعضهم بعضا ورأى تبريه ممن خالفه فرضا وظهرت منهم أمارات المعاداة والتباغض ، كما عرف من فرق المعتزلة والخوارج والروافض ، وما ذلك إلا من من الله عز وجل عليهم وإحسانه في الائتلاف مع وجود الاختلاف إليهم
As for the companions, despite their disagreement in some issues, they are unanimous in refraining from declaring one another disbelievers, contrary to others from all the remaining sects. And all the factions, when odious desires and paths differed among them, declared one another disbelievers and considered it obligatory to disassociate from whoever opposed them. And signs of enmity and mutual hatred appeared from them, as is known from the sects of the Mu'tazila, Khawarij, and Rawafid. And that is nothing but a favor from Allah, the Mighty and Majestic, upon them and His beneficence in (granting) unity despite the existence of disagreement among them.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage highlights a distinctive characteristic of the Ash'ari school: despite internal disagreements on subsidiary matters, they do not engage in takfir of each other. This is contrasted with other sects, such as the Mu'tazila, Khawarij, and Rawafid, who readily declare each other disbelievers upon disagreements. Ibn Asakir presents this as a divine favor and beneficence upon the Ash'aris, allowing them to remain united despite differing views.

Defense of Ash'ari's Scholarly Prominence
Ibn Asakir refutes two accusations against the Ash'ari school.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ibn Asakir refutes the accusation that Ash'ari's doctrine was abandoned and explains its historical continuity and revival through al-Baqillani.

Core Idea
The Ash'ari school was never abandoned; most scholars followed it, and al-Baqillani revived its prominence.

Ibn Asakir defends al-Ash'ari against two accusations: that his doctrine was abandoned, and that it only became popular recently. He provides evidence of widespread adherence among major jurists and explains how Qadi al-Baqillani later brought it to prominence. This passage reveals the historical strength of the Ash'ari school even before al-Baqillani.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the strong refutation tone (e.g., 'zulman wa-zuran'). Identify the two claims Ibn Asakir is answering.
The passage uses rhetorical questions to emphasize the absurdity of the claim.
2
Identify the first refutation
Ibn Asakir counters the claim that Ash'ari's doctrine was abandoned by listing the many scholars who follow it: Hanafis, Malikis, Shafi'is, except a small group of anthropomorphists.
He mentions that the adherents are the ones who issue rulings and clarify matters.
3
Understand the second refutation
The opponent claimed that affiliation to Ash'ari only became strong less than thirty years ago. Ibn Asakir replies that it became famous in the era of al-Baqillani, but that does not mean it was abandoned before.
He also notes that before al-Baqillani, Mu'tazilism was widespread and Sunnis were hiding.
4
Reflect on the historical context
Consider the shift: from Mu'tazili dominance to Ash'ari prominence through al-Baqillani's efforts. This shows the school's resilience.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما قوله لم يزل قول الأشعرى مهجورا . فقد جاء في قوله ظلما وزورا كيف يكون مهجورا وأكثر العلماء في جميع الاقطار عليه ، وأئمة الامصار في سائر الاعصار يدعون إليه ومنتحلوه هم الذين عليهم مدار الأحكام ، وإليهم يرجع في معرفة الحلال والحرام وهم الذين يفتون الناس في صعاب المسائل ، ويعتمد عليهم الخلق في إيضاح المشكلات والنوازل ، وهل من الفقهاء من الحنيفية والمالكية والشافعية إلا موافق له أو منتسب إليه، أو راض بحميد سعيه في دين الله أو مثن بكثرة العلم عليه غير شرذمة يـسـيـرة تـضـمـر التشبيه، وتعادى كل موحد يعتقد التنزيه وتضاهى أقوال أهل الاعتزال في ذمه ، وتباهی باظهار جهلها بقدرة سعة علمه . وقوله أن مذ قوى ذلك أقل من ثلاثين سنة . فلعمرى أنه إنما اشتهرت هذه النسبة من الأزمنة في عصر القاضي أبي بكر بن الباقلاني ذي التصانيف المستحسنة وانتشرت ببغداد وغيرها من البلدان والأمكنة ، وقد ذكرت فيما تقدم أن الانتساب إلى الاعتزال كان فاشياً منتشراً ، وكل من كان متسننا كان متخفياً إلى أن قام القاضى أبو بكر بنصرة المذهب وانتشر عنه في المشرق والمغرب وكان يظهر في دار السلام التي هي قبة الإسلام
And as for his statement: 'The doctrine of al-Ash'ari has never ceased to be abandoned.' He has come in his statement with injustice and falsehood. How could it be abandoned when most scholars in all regions follow it, and the imams of the cities in all ages call to it? Its adherents are those upon whom the rulings (ahkam) revolve, and to them reference is made in knowing the lawful and unlawful. They are the ones who give fatwas to people in difficult issues, and the people rely on them in clarifying problematic matters and new occurrences. Is there any jurist among the Hanafis, Malikis, and Shafi'is except that he is either in agreement with him or affiliated to him, or is content with his praiseworthy striving in the religion of Allah, or praises his abundant knowledge, except for a small handful who conceal anthropomorphism (tashbih), enmity toward every monotheist who affirms transcendence (tanzih), and who imitate the sayings of the Mu'tazila in criticizing him, and who boast of displaying their ignorance of the extent of his knowledge? And as for his statement: 'That (affiliation) has only been strong for less than thirty years.' Upon my life, this affiliation only became famous in times during the era of Qadi Abu Bakr ibn al-Baqillani, author of commendable books, and it spread in Baghdad and other cities and places. I have mentioned previously that affiliation to Mu'tazilism was widespread and prevalent, and whoever was a Sunni was hiding it, until Qadi Abu Bakr arose to support the school, and it spread from him in the East and West, and it became apparent in Dar al-Salam (Baghdad), which is the dome of Islam.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage defends the prominence of the Ash'ari school. Ibn Asakir refutes two claims: first, that Ash'ari's doctrine was abandoned; he lists the many scholars who follow it, including Hanafis, Malikis, and Shafi'is, except a tiny group that secretly holds anthropomorphism. Second, he counters the claim that the affiliation to Ash'ari is recent (less than thirty years) by noting that it became famous in the time of Qadi Abu Bakr al-Baqillani, a later figure, but the school had earlier roots. He also mentions that previously, Mu'tazilism was dominant and Sunnis were hidden, until al-Baqillani revived the Ash'ari school and it spread widely.

مهجورا
التشبيه
التنزيه
القاضي أبو بكر بن الباقلاني
الانتساب إلى الاعتزال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Ash'ari school was obscure and abandoned until al-Baqillani appeared.
Correction: Ibn Asakir shows that the school was always followed by the majority of scholars, and al-Baqillani only made it publicly prominent.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Asakir establishes that the Ash'ari school was always the way of the majority of scholars, and al-Baqillani revived its public prominence.

The Ash'ari Unity: Refraining from Mutual Takfir
Ibn Asakir contrasts Ash'ari unity with sectarian disunity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Ash'ari scholars maintained unity by refraining from declaring each other disbelievers, in contrast to other sects that practiced mutual excommunication.

Core Idea
Ash'ari unity rests on avoiding takfir, not on complete agreement.

Ibn Asakir presents a defining characteristic of the Ash'ari school: despite differences in subsidiary matters, they never excommunicate one another. This passage contrasts their restraint with the mutual takfir of other sects, attributing their harmony to divine favor. Let's read how he makes this point.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Note the contrast Ibn Asakir sets up: 'As for the companions... they are agreed upon refraining from declaring each other disbelievers, unlike those other than them.'
Pay attention to the three sects named: Mu'tazila, Khawarij, Rawafid.
2
Identify the key principle
The central point is that Ash'ari scholars are united on refraining from takfir of one another, even though they differ in some issues. This is a principle of tolerance within the school.
Takfir is declaring someone a disbeliever (kafir).
3
Compare with other sects
Ibn Asakir then describes how other sects, when their opinions diverge, excommunicate each other and consider disassociation an obligation, leading to enmity.
The contrast highlights the Ash'ari approach as more restrained and community-preserving.
4
Reflect on the divine favor
The passage concludes that this unity despite difference is a favor from Allah. This implies that the Ash'ari restraint is not merely a human decision but a grace that protects their community.
Consider how this reinforces the idea of the Ash'ari school as a divinely guided community.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما الأصحاب فإنهم مع اختلافهم في بعض المسائل مجمعون على ترك تكفير بعضهم بعضا بخلاف من عداهم من سائر الطوائف ، وجميع الفرق فإنهم حين اختلفت بهم مستشنعات الأهواء والطرق كفر بعضهم بعضا ورأى تبرية ممن خالفه فرضا وظهرت منهم أمارات المعاداة والتباغض ، كما عرف من فرق المعتزلة والخوارج والروافض ، وما ذلك إلا من من الله عز وجل عليهم وإحسانه في الائتلاف مع وجود الاختلاف إليهم.
As for the companions (the Ash'aris), despite their differences in some issues, they are agreed upon refraining from declaring each other disbelievers, unlike those other than them from the rest of the sects. All the sects, when the repugnant desires and ways differed among them, declared each other disbelievers and considered it an obligation to disavow whoever opposed them, and signs of enmity and mutual hatred appeared from them, as is known from the sects of the Mu'tazila, Khawarij, and Rawafid. And that is nothing but a favor from Allah Almighty and His beneficence upon them in unity despite the existence of difference among them.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage is a comparative defense of the Ash'ari school. Ibn Asakir begins by acknowledging that the Ash'ari scholars differ among themselves in some subsidiary issues. However, they are united in one crucial principle: they do not declare each other disbelievers (takfir) over these differences. This is contrasted with all other sects, such as the Mu'tazila, Khawarij, and Rawafid (Shi'a), who, when their desires and paths become repugnant and divergent, actually excommunicate each other and consider it a religious duty to disassociate from opponents, leading to open enmity and hatred. Ibn Asakir then attributes the Ash'ari unity not to their own merit but to a favor and grace from Allah, who grants them harmony despite the existence of disagreement. The implication is that this unity is a sign of truth and divine support.

Key Terms
أصحاب
تكفير
فرق
معتزلة
خوارج
روافض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that Ash'ari scholars have no differences among themselves.
Correction: This passage explicitly states that they do have differences in some issues, but they refrain from mutual takfir, which is the key to their unity.

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Asakir, what distinguishes the Ash'ari scholars from other sects?
A) They have no differences among themselves.
B) They avoid declaring each other disbelievers despite differences.
C) They declare everyone else disbelievers.
D) They agree on all issues.

Key Takeaway
Ash'ari unity is defined not by the absence of differences, but by the commitment to avoid takfir of one another, which is a divine favor.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you find yourself disagreeing with another Muslim about a matter of religion, does your heart incline towards dismissing them or even silently condemning them? The Ash'aris maintained unity by refusing to declare each other disbelievers. In your own life, where can you begin to practice this restraint, even when you feel strongly that you are right?
?
The passage says that the Ash'ari unity is a favor from Allah, not a human achievement. Do you truly believe that your ability to stay united with others who differ from you comes from Allah? If so, what does that demand from you in terms of humility and gratitude, especially when you are tempted to feel superior?

Defense of the Ash'ari School's Dominance
Ibn Asakir refutes the accusation of Ash'ari obscurity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ibn Asakir defends the widespread acceptance of the Ash'ari school by refuting the claim of its obscurity.

Core Idea
The Ash'ari school was never obscure; it was followed by the majority of scholars.

In this passage, Ibn Asakir responds to a critic who claimed that al-Ash'ari's doctrine was abandoned and marginalized. Using rhetorical questions and evidence from the scholarly community, he demonstrates that the Ash'ari school was in fact the dominant creed among the major Sunni legal schools. This lesson will explore his argument and the historical reality he presents.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the English translation to grasp the overall argument.
Notice the strong rhetorical language Ibn Asakir uses.
2
Identify the opponent's claim
Find the statement attributed to the critic and see how Ibn Asakir immediately dismisses it as false.
3
Examine the evidence
List the pieces of evidence Ibn Asakir provides for the widespread acceptance of al-Ash'ari's doctrine.
He mentions scholars, imams, legal authorities, and the three major madhhabs.
4
Understand the exception
Note the small group that rejects al-Ash'ari and their characteristics, according to Ibn Asakir.
This exception proves the rule of dominance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما قوله لم يزل قول الأشعري مهجورا . فقد جاء في قوله ظلما وزورا كيف يكون مهجورا وأكثر العلماء في جميع الاقطار عليه ، وأئمة الامصار في سائر الاعصار يدعون إليه ومنتحلوه هم الذين عليهم مدار الأحكام ، وإليهم يرجع في معرفة الحلال والحرام وهم الذين يفتون الناس في صعاب المسائل ، ويعتمد عليهم الخلق في إيضاح المشكلات والنوازل ، وهل من الفقهاء من الحنيفية والمالكية والشافعية إلا موافق له أو منتسب إليه، أو راض بحميد سعيه في دين الله أو مثن بكثرة العلم عليه غير شرذمة يسيرة تضمر التشبيه، وتعادى كل موحد يعتقد التنزيه وتضاهى أقوال أهل الاعتزال في ذمه ، وتباهي باظهار جهلها بقدرة سعة علمه .
And as for his statement: 'The saying of al-Ash'ari has not ceased to be abandoned.' He has come in his statement with injustice and falsehood. How could it be abandoned when the majority of scholars in all regions are upon it? The imams of the cities in all ages call to it. Its adherents are those upon whom revolve the rulings (ahkam), and to them reference is made in knowledge of the lawful and unlawful. They are the ones who issue fatwas to people in difficult matters, and the creation relies on them in clarifying problems and new occurrences. Is there any of the jurists among the Hanafis, Malikis, and Shafi'is except that he is either in agreement with him, or affiliated to him, or satisfied with his praiseworthy effort in the religion of Allah, or praising him for the abundance of knowledge, except for a small band that harbors anthropomorphism (tashbih), and is hostile to every monotheist who believes in transcendence (tanzih), and emulates the sayings of the people of i'tizal in disparaging him, and boasts in showing its ignorance of the extent of his knowledge.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage refutes the claim that al-Ash'ari's doctrine was always abandoned. Ibn Asakir calls this claim unjust and false. He argues that most scholars across all regions and ages are upon the Ash'ari creed. The imams of cities call to it. The adherents of this school are those who are the authority in legal rulings (ahkam) and are consulted for halal and haram. They are the muftis in difficult matters and the ones people rely on for solving problems and new issues. Then he asks rhetorically: Is there any Hanafi, Maliki, or Shafi'i jurist who does not agree with him, or affiliate with him, or approve of his good efforts, or praise his abundant knowledge? The only exception is a small group that secretly anthropomorphize God (tashbih), are hostile to those who affirm tanzih (transcendence), and imitate the Mu'tazila in their criticism while boasting about their ignorance.

Key Terms
مهجور
حنيفية
مالكية
شافعية
تشبيه
تنزيه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Ash'ari school was always a minority and obscure.
Correction: Ibn Asakir shows that it was actually the dominant school among Hanafis, Malikis, and Shafi'is across regions and eras, with only a small fringe opposing it.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which groups of jurists generally accept al-Ash'ari's teaching?
A) Only Shafi'is.
B) Only Hanafis and Malikis.
C) Hanafis, Malikis, and Shafi'is, with few exceptions.
D) None of them.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Asakir's defense proves that the Ash'ari school was the mainstream creed of Sunni Islam, not a marginalized sect.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have seen that Ibn Asakir vigorously defends the mainstream creed. Are you content to follow the majority of scholars, or do you find yourself drawn to fringe views that appeal to your ego or desire for uniqueness? What is the condition of your heart when you hear someone disparage the 'aqidah of the majority? Will you defend the truth even if it means opposing a vocal minority, or do you remain silent out of fear of conflict?
?
This passage shows that the Ash'ari school was integral to Islamic jurisprudence and daily life. Does your own 'aqidah shape your understanding of halal and haram, or have you compartmentalized theology from practice? Commit today to study the 'aqidah that the majority of scholars upheld, so that your actions are grounded in sound belief.

Ibn Asakir's Rebuttal: False Refuters Only Harm Themselves
Ibn Asakir rebuts the idea that every land has someone who refutes the Ash'aris.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ibn Asakir's rebuttal of the claim that every region has a refuter of Ash'aris, and why he says such refuters only harm themselves.

Core Idea
False refuters only deceive the ignorant and harm themselves.

Ibn Asakir is addressing a common accusation against the Ash'ari school. In this passage, he turns the tables on the accuser, arguing that the so-called refuters in every region are not true scholars but ignorant speakers who only mislead the simple-minded. Let's read his sharp response.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once and then its literal translation. Notice the opponent's claim and Ibn Asakir's response.
Pay attention to the word 'يدحض' (refutes) and its usage.
2
Understand the reversal
Identify Ibn Asakir's logical move: he suggests that if the opponent said the opposite—that every region lacks a true refuter—that would be true. Why? Because the supposed refuters are not armed with sound evidence.
The Arabic phrase 'يخلو كل قطر من قائم منهم بالحجة' is key.
3
Examine the description of false refuters
Look at how Ibn Asakir characterizes those who claim to refute without knowledge: they are speakers without correctness, following faults, harming only themselves and deceiving the foolish.
Note terms like 'معطلة' (negators) and 'مشبهة' (anthropomorphists).
4
Reflect on the warning
Consider the lesson for the reader: to beware of those who speak without knowledge and to recognize that true evidence is with the Ash'ari scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما قوله أن الله لا يخلي كل قطر ممن يدحض قولهم ويبين فضيحتهم ويدمغ كلمتهم . فلو عكس ما قاله فى ذلك لصدق قوله ، ولم يتهم لأنه يخلو كل قطر من قائم منهم بالحجة موضح للناس سبيل المحجة مبين للخلق تمويهات المموهة ، محذر من مذاهب المعطلة والمشبهة ، وإن كان كل عصر لا يخلو من قائل بغير علم ومتكلم بغير إصابة ولا فهم مشتمل على أنواع من المعايب ، مقتد بفعله في تصنيف المثالب غير أنه لا يضر بما يتقول من البهتان إلا خاصة نفسه ولا يغر إلا غماراً إذا اعتبرتهم وجدتهم من جنسه.
And as for his statement: 'Allah does not leave any region devoid of someone who refutes their saying, exposes their disgrace, and smashes their word.' If he reversed what he said in that, his statement would be true and not suspect, because every region is devoid of one among them who stands with the evidence, clarifying to the people the path of the clear way, explaining to the creation the camouflage of the camouflagers, warning against the doctrines of the negators (mu'attila) and anthropomorphists (mushabbiha). Even if every age is not devoid of a speaker without knowledge and a talker without correctness or understanding, one who includes types of faults, following his action in classifying faults, he does not harm by what he utters of slander except his own self, and he only deceives the foolish; if you consider them, you find them of his kind.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage refutes the claim that in every region there is someone who refutes the Ash'ari position. Ibn Asakir says that if the accuser reversed his statement—meaning that every region does have an Ash'ari who stands with clear evidence—then he would be truthful. But actually, every region is empty of such a refuter. Instead, every age does have ignorant speakers who talk without knowledge, but they only harm themselves by their slander and only deceive the simple-minded, who are of their own kind.

Key Terms
يدحض
معطلة
مشبهة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think there are many effective refuters of Ash'aris across regions.
Correction: The passage argues that such refuters are not armed with evidence and only harm themselves and deceive the ignorant.

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Asakir, what is the effect of the false refuters?
A) They harm the Ash'ari school.
B) They only harm themselves and deceive the foolish.
C) They convince the scholars.
D) They strengthen their own position.

Key Takeaway
True refutation requires sound knowledge; those who speak without it only harm themselves.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you speak about matters of faith, do you ensure you have solid knowledge, or do you sometimes rely on what you've heard without verification? How does Ibn Asakir's warning about harming only yourself apply to your own speech?
?
Have you ever been quick to dismiss a group or person based on accusations from others? This passage reminds us that true refuters are rare. How can you guard against being deceived by the foolish or becoming one who speaks without understanding?
?
Ibn Asakir says false refuters only harm themselves. Reflect on a time you spoke carelessly about a religious issue. Did it lead to regret or unintended consequences? What would it take for you to commit to speaking only with knowledge and evidence?

Refutation of Ahwazi's Claim: Every Region Has a Truth-Defender
Ibn Asakir reverses Ahwazi's claim and clarifies the state of truth-defenders.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ibn Asakir reverses Ahwazi's claim about God's provision of truth-defenders and affirms the constant presence of proof and guidance everywhere.

Core Idea
Ahwazi's claim, when reversed, reveals the truth: every region has a defender of truth.

Ibn Asakir critiques Ahwazi's statement that Allah leaves no region without someone who refutes falsehood. He argues that if Ahwazi had simply reversed his wording, his claim would be accurate: rather, every region has a person who stands with clear proof and warns against deviant sects. He then acknowledges the existence of false claimants but notes they only harm themselves.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let Ibn Asakir's argument flow naturally.
Notice the structure: quotation, reversal, concession.
2
Identify the reversal
Ibn Asakir quotes Ahwazi's claim and then says 'He should have reversed what he said...' Find the exact reversal and understand the correction.
The reversal changes 'no region without a refuter' to 'every region has a proofer.'
3
Understand the concession
Ibn Asakir admits there are ignorant speakers, but explains they only harm themselves and deceive their own kind. Why does he include this point?
This strengthens his argument by acknowledging reality while undermining the opponent's implication.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما قوله ( أن الله لا يخلى كل قطر ممن يدحض قولهم ويبين فضيحتهم ويدمغ كلمتهم . فلو عكس ما قاله فى ذلك لصدق قوله ، ولم يتهم لأنه يخلو كل قطر من قائم منهم بالحجة موضح للناس سبيل المحجة مبين للخلق تمويهات المموهة ، محذر من مذاهب المعطلة والمشبهة ، وإن كان كل عصر لا يخلو من قائل بغير علم ومتكلم بغير إصابة ولا فهم مشتمل على أنواع من المعايب ، مقتد بفعله في تصنيف المثالب غير أنه لا يضر بما يتقول من البهتان إلا خاصة نفسه ولا يغر إلا غماراً إذا اعتبرتهم وجدتهم من جنسه.
As for his statement: 'Allah does not leave any region without someone who nullifies their statement, exposes their disgrace, and refutes their word.' He should have reversed what he said in that to be truthful and not accused, because every region has someone who stands with the proof, clarifying to the people the path of the clear way, explaining to the creation the deceptions of the misrepresenters, warning against the doctrines of the Mu'attila and the Mushabbiha. And although every age is not free from a speaker without knowledge and a speaker without correctness or understanding, encompassing types of faults, following his deed in composing defects, yet he harms none by the falsehood he fabricates except his own self, and he deceives only the ignorant; if you consider them, you find them of his kind.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of Ahwazi's claim that Allah does not leave any region without a person who refutes falsehood. Ibn Asakir argues that if Ahwazi had reversed his statement, it would be true: rather, every region has a person who stands with clear proof, clarifies the path, exposes deceptions, and warns against the deviant sects (the Mu'attila who deny attributes and the Mushabbiha who anthropomorphize). Ibn Asakir then concedes that in every age there are ignorant speakers who fabricate falsehoods, but they only harm themselves and deceive their own kind. The point is that while false claimants exist, the true defenders of truth are present everywhere, contrary to Ahwazi's intended implication that only falsehood is defended.

Key Terms
المعطلة
المشبهة
بهتان
بالحجة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Allah leaves some regions without a truth-defender, implying falsehood dominates.
Correction: In reality, every region has a truth-defender; false claimants are present but harmless and self-limiting.

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Asakir, what does every region actually have?
A) A person who refutes falsehood and guides to truth
B) A person who fabricates lies and misleads
C) No one who defends the truth
D) Only ignorant speakers

Key Takeaway
Ibn Asakir demonstrates that Ahwazi's claim, when reversed, affirms that every region has a clear defender of truth, while false claimants only harm themselves.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you a defender of truth in your community, standing with clear proof and warning against falsehood, or do you remain silent while others spread error? What step will you take today to become a clear guide for those seeking truth?
?
The lesson warns that false claimants speak without knowledge and only harm themselves. Think of a time you spoke about Islam without proper understanding. Did it harm your faith or mislead others? How can you ensure you speak only with proof and certainty from now on?
?
If you consider those around you, do you find more truth-defenders or false claimants? What is your role in tipping the balance? Are you willing to be the one who clarifies and warns, even if it costs you comfort or popularity?
